Net interest income rose 15.41% to Rs 2,807 crore.</p></li></ul></div><div style="color: #44475b; font-weight: 500; font-size: 28px; line-height: 24px; margin: 44px 0px 30px;"><span style="font-size: 18pt;">Word of the Day</span></div><div style="color: #44475b; border: 1px solid grey; border-radius: 8px; text-align: center; width: 400px; max-width: 100%; margin: 0px auto 28px;"><div style="font-weight: 600; font-size: 20px; line-height: 24px; margin-top: 28px;"><span style="font-size: 12pt;"><span style="font-family: 'Open Sans', sans-serif;"><span style="font-size: 14pt; color: #000000;">Leveraged Buyout</span></span><br><br></span></div><div style="width: 100%; height: 0px; border-top: 1px solid grey;"><br></div><div style="font-weight: 400; padding: 32px; text-align: center; font-size: 16px; line-height: 22px;"><p>A Leveraged Buyout (LBO) happens when a company is purchased using a loan.</p></div></div><div style="color: #44475b; font-weight: 400; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 22px; margin-bottom: 16px;"><p>Let's take the case of company ABC, which wants to acquire a company called XYZ.</p><p>But ABC does not have enough money to do that.&nbsp;So, it takes a loan and acquires company XYZ.</p><p>This is an example of a 'leveraged buyout'.</p><p>In finance, 'leverage' refers to using loans.&nbsp;</p><p>Such buyouts are uncommon in India due to regulations.</p><p>In the past, some Indian companies have used leverage to acquire foreign companies.</p><p>Example: Tata Tea's buyout of Tetley in 2000.</p></div><div style="color: #44475b; font-weight: 500; font-size: 28px; line-height: 24px; margin: 44px 0px 30px;"><span style="font-size: 18pt;">6 Day Course</span></div><div style="color: #44475b; font-weight: 500; font-size: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px; line-height: 24px;"><span style="font-size: 12pt;">Theme: qualities of good mutual funds</span></div><div style="color: #44475b; width: 100%; height: 0px; border-top: 1px solid grey; margin-bottom: 10px;"><br></div><!--Tuesday Start--><div style="font-weight: 500; font-size: 14px; line-height: 24px;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="margin: 0px 10px;">Mon</span><span style="margin: 0px 10px; background: #44475b; color: white; border: 1px solid #44475b; border-radius: 30px; padding: 4px 8px;">Tue</span><span style="margin: 0px 10px; color: #a1a3ad;">Wed</span><span style="margin: 0px 10px; color: #a1a3ad;">Thu</span><span style="margin: 0px 10px; color: #a1a3ad;">Fri</span><span style="margin: 0px 10px; color: #a1a3ad;">Sun</span></span></div><!--Tuesday End--><div style="color: #44475b; width: 100%; height: 0px; border-top: 1px solid grey; margin-top: 10px;"><br></div><div style="color: #44475b; font-weight: 400; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 22px; margin: 20px 0px 16px;"><p>Returns.</p><p>This is something everyone does — looking at past returns of mutual funds.</p><p>This is a good strategy. But there are some key factors to note.</p><p>First: past returns do not guarantee future returns.</p><p>A mutual fund has given 20% in the last 1 year. This does not mean it will give 20% in the next year too.</p><p>Second: short term returns are not as useful. Long term returns are more useful.</p><p>Many investors look at mutual funds’ last 1 year returns and make an investment.</p><p>This is usually a bad strategy.</p><p>Looking at a mutual funds’ long term returns gives us a better understanding of its performance and capability.</p><p>Example: checking returns of last 5 years, 7 years, 10 years, etc.</p></div><div style="color: #44475b; width: 5%; height: 0px; border-top: 3px solid black; margin: 24px 0px 16px;"><br></div><div style="color: #7c7e8c; font-style: italic; margin-bottom: 20px; font-weight: 400; font-size: 14px; line-height: 20px;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Missed last week's course? You can download the course PDF - <a href="https://groww.weurl.co/lw/g1.jpg?p=eyJsYyI6Imlufjc2YWEzOTIiLCJsIjoiN2QzZDM3NTM0NWJiNzMxYjg1ZmQ3NzIxMDBmZWNkNDMiLCJjIjoiYjZhNDc2ZGUtOGIyMi00ZTViLWFkNTctYTlmNTljZjgwMjMzIiwiZW0iOiJzdW1lZGhhZ2F0QGdtYWlsLmNvbSIsImUiOiJ%2BMWRuaDJoZiIsInYiOiJ%2BaTJjbjY0IiwicyI6In41MDVhM2RkODg4NTNkMTJfNzc3NGM5ZTMtZTQwMy00YzE3LWI2YzYtNDllZDlkNmVkMzE2OjE3MjkwMDEwODExMzMiLCJldmVudCI6ImVtYWlsX2NsaWNrIiwiY3RhIjoifmJjMzBhZWViIiwidG9VUkwiOiJodHRwczovL2JpdC5seS8zWlhNWndEIn0%3D">click to download</a></span></div><div style="color: #44475b; font-weight: 500; font-size: 28px; line-height: 24px; margin: 44px 0px 28px;"><span style="font-size: 18pt;">Featured Question</span></div><table style="color: #44475b;"><tbody><tr><td style="width: 20%; max-width: 180px;"></td><td style="border: 1px solid #7c7e8c; border-radius: 12px 12px 0px; padding: 20px 16px; font-weight: 500; font-size: 16px; line-height: 20px;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Q. “Are mutual funds allowed to trade the pooled money in the derivatives market like options and futures?”<br></span></td></tr></tbody></table><div style="color: #44475b; border: 1px solid #e9e9eb; border-radius: 12px 12px 12px 0px; padding: 20px 16px; margin: 20px 0px; width: 70%; max-width: 420px;"><div style="font-weight: 400; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 22px; margin-bottom: 16px; color: #44475b;">A.&nbsp;<span style="font-size: 11pt;">There are many restrictions on mutual funds investing in derivatives. The regulator carefully monitors such activity too.</span><p>But technically, yes — it is allowed.</p><p>In practice, most mutual fund managers do not use derivatives a lot, only in limited quantities.</p><p>Some mutual funds may use these options more than others — but even that is relatively low.</p><p>Equity mutual funds mostly invest using long-term strategies.</p></div></div><div style="color: #44475b; width: 5%; height: 0px; border-top: 3px solid black; margin: 24px 0px 16px;"><br></div><div style="color: #7c7e8c; font-style: italic; margin-bottom: 8px; font-weight: 400; font-size: 14px; line-height: 20px;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">In this section, daily, we'll try to answer one burning question related to the field of personal finance education.</span></div><div style="color: #7c7e8c; font-weight: 500; font-size: 28px; line-height: 24px; margin: 44px 0px 30px;"><span style="font-size: 18pt;">Word of the Day</span></div><div style="color: #44475b; border: 1px solid grey; border-radius: 8px; text-align: center; width: 400px; max-width: 100%; margin: 0px auto 28px;"><div style="font-weight: 600; font-size: 20px; line-height: 24px; margin-top: 28px;"><span style="font-size: 12pt;"><span style="font-family: 'Open Sans', sans-serif;"><span style="font-size: 14pt; color: #000000;">Dead Cat Bounce</span></span><br><br></span></div><div style="width: 100%; height: 0px; border-top: 1px solid grey;"><br></div><div style="font-weight: 400; padding: 32px; text-align: center; font-size: 16px; line-height: 22px;"><p>A dead cat bounce refers to a temporary rise in a stock's price after a continuous decline.</p></div></div><div style="color: #44475b; font-weight: 400; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 22px; margin-bottom: 16px;"><p>After the bounce, the stock usually continues its downward trend.</p><p>The term originates from the phrase, “Even a dead cat will bounce if dropped from a height.”</p><p>It tricks some people into thinking the stock is recovering but usually falls again shortly after.</p><p>A dead cat bounce is a price pattern that is usually recognized in hindsight.</p></div><div style="color: #44475b; font-weight: 500; font-size: 28px; line-height: 24px; margin: 44px 0px 30px;"><span style="font-size: 18pt;">6 Day Course</span></div><div style="color: #44475b; font-weight: 500; font-size: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px; line-height: 24px;"><span style="font-size: 12pt;">Theme: qualities of good mutual funds&nbsp;</span></div><div style="color: #44475b; width: 100%; height: 0px; border-top: 1px solid grey; margin-bottom: 10px;"><br></div><!--Monday Start--><div style="font-weight: 500; font-size: 14px; line-height: 24px;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="margin: 0px; background: #44475b; color: white; border: 1px solid #44475b; border-radius: 30px; padding: 4px 8px;">Mon</span><span style="margin: 0px 10px; color: #a1a3ad;">Tue</span><span style="margin: 0px 10px; color: #a1a3ad;">Wed</span><span style="margin: 0px 10px; color: #a1a3ad;">Thu</span><span style="margin: 0px 10px; color: #a1a3ad;">Fri</span><span style="margin: 0px 10px; color: #a1a3ad;">Sun</span></span></div><!--Monday End--><div style="color: #44475b; width: 100%; height: 0px; border-top: 1px solid grey; margin-top: 10px;"><br></div><div style="color: #44475b; font-weight: 400; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 22px; margin: 20px 0px 16px;"><p>Many times, investors struggle to choose the right mutual funds.</p><p>In this week’s course, we will try to understand some of the qualities of good mutual funds.</p><p>One of the qualities is a good track record.</p><p>Older mutual funds have a longer performance history that can be analysed.&nbsp;</p><p>This does not mean all older mutual funds are better.</p><p>A longer track record might not necessarily be good. A fund that has existed for 10 years might have performed poorly over that period, too.</p><p>However, a mutual fund that has been around for a few years would have seen good periods (when markets are going up) and bad periods (when markets are crashing).</p><p>This allows us to check how the mutual fund has reacted under different market conditions.</p></div><div style="color: #44475b; width: 5%; height: 0px; border-top: 3px solid black; margin: 24px 0px 16px;"><br></div><div style="color: #7c7e8c; font-style: italic; margin-bottom: 20px; font-weight: 400; font-size: 14px; line-height: 20px;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Missed last week's course? font-weight: 500; font-size: 28px; line-height: 24px; margin: 44px 0px 28px;"><span style="font-size: 18pt;">Featured Question</span></div><table style="color: #44475b;"><tbody><tr><td style="width: 20%; max-width: 180px;"></td><td style="border: 1px solid #7c7e8c; border-radius: 12px 12px 0px; padding: 20px 16px; font-weight: 500; font-size: 16px; line-height: 20px;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Q. “What is difference between market return and portfolio return”<br></span></td></tr></tbody></table><div style="color: #44475b; border: 1px solid #e9e9eb; border-radius: 12px 12px 12px 0px; padding: 20px 16px; margin: 20px 0px; width: 70%; max-width: 420px;"><div style="font-weight: 400; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 22px; margin-bottom: 16px; color: #44475b;">A.&nbsp;<span style="font-size: 11pt;">Market return = returns given by the stock markets.</span><p>The term market can mean different things to different investors.</p><p>Example: for many people, “markets” is Nifty 50.</p><p>For some others, Sensex 30, Nifty 100, etc might mean “markets”.</p><p>So, say Nifty 50 has increased at a rate of 15% per annum over the last 5 years.</p><p>So, we can say that the market's returns have been 15% per annum over the last 5 years.</p><p>Portfolio returns usually refer to your personal investment's returns.</p><p>Say you have invested in different stocks, mutual funds, FD, etc.</p><p>How much have they grown?</p><p>That’s your portfolio returns.</p><p>Example: someone’s portfolio returns may be 10% per annum over the last 5 years.</p></div></div><div style="color: #44475b; ** Welcome to CannaGlobe’s Weekly Hit, your preferred guide to the world of good health through
------------------------------------------------------------


** Cannabis and Mushrooms.
------------------------------------------------------------


** Human Endocannabinoid System
------------------------------------------------------------

After 35 years of research, scientists have only just begun to understand the importance of the Human Endocannabinoid System (HEcS). The discovery of the HEcS is arguably the most important discovery in human physiology in the late Twentieth Century. Research has revealed that the HEcS is responsible for maintaining and controlling the body’s homeostasis, or balanced regulation of every system in the body. It does that through two known receptors called CB1 & CB2.

While the body produces its own endogenous cannabinoids, many scientists suggest that most people are now suffering from “Cannabinoid Deficiency”. Without sufficient cannabinoids in our diet, the HEcS operates at less than peak efficiency, resulting in a general decline in overall health. Supplementing our diets with full spectrum phytocannabinoids may be an essential component to achieving optimal health.


** Endocannabinoid System
------------------------------------------------------------

The Endocannabinoid System is found in every animal, except for insects, and regulates a broad range of biological functions. The ECS is a biochemical control system of neuromodulatory lipids (molecules that include fats, waxes, sterols and fat-soluble vitamins such as vitamins A, D, E and K and others) and specialized receptors configured to accept certain cannabinoids. In general, a given receptor will accept only particular classes of compounds and will be unaffected by other compounds, just as a specific key is needed to open a lock.

Specialized receptors are located throughout the human body, including but not limited to, in the hippocampus (memory, learning), the cerebral cortex (decision-making, emotional behavior), the cerebellum (motor control, coordination), putamen (movement, learning), the hypothalamus (appetite, body temperature) and the amygdala (emotions). When a specific cannabinoid or combination of cannabinoids bind to a specialized receptor, an event or a series of events, is triggered in the cell, resulting in a change in the cell’s activity, its gene regulation and/or the signals that it sends to neighboring cells. This process is called “signal transduction.”

First detected in the brain, science now shows that CB1-R are also located in many other organs, connective tissues, gonads and glands. CB1-R are not found in the medulla oblongata (the part of the brain stem responsible for respiratory and cardiovascular functions). CB1-R play an important role in the coordination of movements, spatial orientation, sensory perceptions (taste, touch, smell, hearing), cognitive performance and motivation.

The most important function of the CB1-R is the reduction of excessive or inadequate signaling by the neurotransmitters (messengers) in the brain. By the activation of the CB1-R, the hyperactivity or hypoactivity of the messengers (e.g., serotonin, dopamine) is regulated back into balance. For example, when THC binds to CB1-R, activity in the pain circuits is inhibited, thus resulting in reduced pain. Many other symptoms such as nausea, muscle spasticity and seizures can be alleviated or diminished with cannabinoid therapy.

CB2-R are primarily associated with the immune system and found outside of the brain in such places as the gut, spleen, liver, heart, kidneys, bones, blood vessels, lymph cells, endocrine glands and reproductive organs. For example, CBD is keyed to CB2-R, and good evidence shows CBD is a beneficial therapeutic strategy to lessen the impact of inflammatory and neuro-inflammatory diseases. Until recently, it was believed that CB-2R played no role with nerve cells or bundles. However, studies now show that it also plays an important role in the signal processing of the brain.

A third receptor that gets little attention is the transient receptor potential vanilloid-type one (TRPV1). The function of TRPV1 is to detect and regulate body temperature. In addition, TRPV1 is responsible for the sensations of extreme external heat and pain and is subject to desensitization. Therefore, if continuously stimulated, the pathway will eventually slow down or even stop. This raises therapeutic possibilities for agents to effectively treat certain kinds of neuropathic pain.

Content Source: MedicalJane.com. Included for educational purposes only.


** CB1 AND CB2 RECEPTORS
------------------------------------------------------------

The primary cannabinoid receptors are identified as Cannabinoid Type 1 receptors (CB1-R) and Cannabinoid Type 2 receptors (CB2-R). The receptors can be “unlocked” by three kinds of cannabinoids:


** 1) Endocannabinoids
------------------------------------------------------------

Endogenous-fatty-acid cannabinoids produced naturally in the body (eg. anandamide and 2-AG)


** 2) Phytocannabinoids
------------------------------------------------------------

Concentrated in the oily resin of the buds and leaves of plants such as cannabis (eg. THC and CBD)


** 3) Synthetic Cannabinoids
------------------------------------------------------------

Manufactured by artificial means such as in a laboratory

3 reasons to consider studying an online master’s degree

Are you considering furthering your education but unsure about the format?

Discover why an online master's degree might be the perfect fit for you! In our latest article, we explore 3 compelling reasons to pursue an online master's program, highlighting its flexibility and quality.

With advances in technology, online learning offers an educational experience that rivals traditional on-campus programs. Designed to accommodate your schedule and personal commitments, this format is especially advantageous for busy professionals looking to advance their careers.

Learn more about how an online master’s could open doors and enhance your professional prospects.

border: 1px solid grey; border-radius: 8px; text-align: center; width: 400px; max-width: 100%; margin: 0px auto 28px;"><div style="font-weight: 600; font-size: 20px; line-height: 24px; margin-top: 28px;"><span style="font-size: 12pt;"><span style="font-family: 'Open Sans', sans-serif;"><span style="font-size: 14pt; color: #000000;">Insurance Float</span></span><br><br></span></div><div style="width: 100%; height: 0px; border-top: 1px solid grey;"><br></div><div style="font-weight: 400; padding: 32px; text-align: center; font-size: 16px; line-height: 22px;"><p>Insurance float refers to money collected from premiums that is held before claims are paid out.</p></div></div><div style="color: #44475b; font-weight: 400; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 22px; margin-bottom: 16px;"><p>The amount received from premiums (also called float) is used to invest in various assets to generate income.</p><p>The time lag between receiving premiums and paying claims allows insurers to keep the float invested for long periods.</p></div><div style="color: #44475b; font-weight: 500; font-size: 28px; line-height: 24px; margin: 44px 0px 30px;"><span style="font-size: 18pt;">6 Day Course</span></div><div style="color: #44475b; font-weight: 500; font-size: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px; line-height: 24px;"><span style="font-size: 12pt;">Theme: different kinds loans </span></div><div style="color: #44475b; width: 100%; height: 0px; border-top: 1px solid grey; margin-bottom: 10px;"><br></div><!--Wednesday Start--><div style="font-weight: 500; font-size: 14px; line-height: 24px;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="margin: 0px 10px;">Mon</span><span style="margin: 0px 10px;">Tue</span><span style="margin: 0px 10px; background: #44475b; color: white; border: 1px solid #44475b; border-radius: 30px; padding: 4px 8px;">Wed</span><span style="margin: 0px 10px; color: #a1a3ad;">Thu</span><span style="margin: 0px 10px; color: #a1a3ad;">Fri</span><span style="margin: 0px 10px; color: #a1a3ad;">Sun</span></span></div><!--Wednesday End--><div style="color: #44475b; width: 100%; height: 0px; border-top: 1px solid grey; margin-top: 10px;"><br></div><div style="color: #44475b; font-weight: 400; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 22px; margin: 20px 0px 16px;"><p>Continuing where we left off yesterday.</p><p>Loans are available against investments too.</p><p>Loans against FD: in this case, the person with an FD can take a loan from the same bank.</p><p>This amount can be used for business or personal use.</p><p>Loans against mutual funds: this option is available too. A bank or NBFC may give loans if you pledge the mutual fund units to them.</p><p>The mutual fund company itself usually does not give the loans.</p><p>Some mutual fund companies have arrangements with banks/NBFCs to make this process easier.</p><p>Loans against insurance policies: similarly, some banks/NBFCs also offer loans against insurance policies.</p><p>Do note, not all insurance policies are allowed in this scheme.</p></div><div style="color: #44475b; width: 5%; height: 0px; border-top: 3px solid black; margin: 24px 0px 16px;"><br></div><div style="color: #7c7e8c; font-style: italic; margin-bottom: 20px; font-weight: 400; font-size: 14px; line-height: 20px;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Missed last week's course? You can download the course PDF - <a href="https://groww.weurl.co/lw/g1.jpg?p=eyJsYyI6Imlufjc2YWEzOTIiLCJsIjoiN2QzZDM3NTM0NWJiNzMxYjg1ZmQ3NzIxMDBmZWNkNDMiLCJjIjoiYjZhNDc2ZGUtOGIyMi00ZTViLWFkNTctYTlmNTljZjgwMjMzIiwiZW0iOiJzdW1lZGhhZ2F0QGdtYWlsLmNvbSIsImUiOiIyazcyN2g4IiwidiI6In4yMmwxNmsxIiwicyI6In4xZjNkZWphMjBmY2FqMV9iYTU4YjRiMS0wMTRmLTQ2NWItYTc3MS02MjEyMGNiMTkyYzY6MTcyODQ4MzcwNDMyNyIsImV2ZW50IjoiZW1haWxfY2xpY2siLCJjdGEiOiIyNGQ2MmRkYSIsInRvVVJMIjoiaHR0cHM6Ly9iaXQubHkvNGV1S01OQyJ9">click to download</a></span></div><div style="color: #44475b; font-weight: 500; font-size: 28px; line-height: 24px; margin: 44px 0px 28px;"><span style="font-size: 18pt;">Featured Question</span></div><table style="color: #44475b;"><tbody><tr><td style="width: 20%; max-width: 180px;"></td><td style="border: 1px solid #7c7e8c; border-radius: 12px 12px 0px; padding: 20px 16px; font-weight: 500; font-size: 16px; line-height: 20px;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Q. “After the death of mutual fund investor what will be done with there investment ?”<br></span></td></tr></tbody></table><div style="color: #44475b; border: 1px solid #e9e9eb; border-radius: 12px 12px 12px 0px; padding: 20px 16px; margin: 20px 0px; width: 70%; max-width: 420px;"><div style="font-weight: 400; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 22px; margin-bottom: 16px; color: #44475b;">A. T<span style="font-size: 11pt;">he mutual fund units can be claimed by the nominee (if the investor had given a nominee/nominees).</span><p>Mutual fund investors can add one or more nominees.</p><p>Mutual fund investors can even allocate different percentages to different nominees.</p><p>Example: 40% to spouse, 30% to parents, 15% to elder child, 15% younger child.</p><p>It makes it easier for the nominees to claim the amount.</p><p>If there is no nominee or if there is a dispute, the mutual fund company will want a legal heir certificate (or a similar court document).</p><p>This document is made by the court stating who will get the mutual fund units.</p><p>The mutual fund company will give the mutual fund units based on this court document (legal heir certificate, or succession certificate, etc).</p><p>In case a nominee name is given in the mutual fund, the process to claim the mutual fund units is much easier than making any court certificate.</p><p>This is why it is necessary to add a nominee/nominees to mutual fund investments.</p></div></div><div style="color: #44475b; Question: What do I do if I forgot to notify USCIS of a change of address?
